These are sales comparison, allocation, extraction, subdivision development, land residual, and ground rent capitalization. The sales comparison approach is the most common and preferred method when sufficient market data is available. The appraiser has sufficient comparable market data, and therefore will rely solely on the sales comparison approach in deriving a unit value. [California Code of Civil Procedure §1263.430]", type='text'), Chunk(id='08a7ecbf-f2fb-4f35-b394-0bf0348fdaf5', grounding=ChunkGrounding(box=ParseGroundingBox(bottom=0.39691123366355896, left=0.1546359360218048, right=0.9390882253646851, top=0.23014792799949646), page=32), markdown="<a id='08a7ecbf-f2fb-4f35-b394-0bf0348fdaf5'></a>\n\nComparable Sales\nWhen relevant to the determination of the value of property, a witness may take into account as a basis for his opinion the price and other terms and circumstances of any sale or contract to sell and purchase comparable property if the sale or contract was freely made in good faith within a reasonable time before or after the date of valuation. In order to be considered comparable, the sale or contract must have been made sufficiently near in time to the date of valuation, and the property sold must be located sufficiently near the property being valued, and must be sufficiently alike in respect to character, size, situation, usability, and improvements, to make it clear that the property sold and the property being valued are comparable in value and that the price realized for the property sold may fairly be considered as shedding light on the value of the property being valued. The subject and the comparable sales relied upon in making said appraisal were as represented by the photographs contained in said appraisal.\n\n<a id=\'a02b06ab-1111-47ee-9989-33efbf727784\'></a>\n\nThat to the best of my knowledge and belief, the statements contained in the appraisal herein set forth are true, and the information upon which the opinions expressed therein are based is correct, subject to limiting conditions therein set forth.\n\n<a id=\'7b23b210-87c6-44be-8a86-0ec28c090745\'></a>\n\nThat I understand that such appraisal is to be used in connection with the acquisition of right of way for a highway to be constructed by the State of California with the assistance of Federal-aid highway funds, or other Federal funds.\n\n<a id=\'255cd396-f9f0-41e4-bf65-00c33a51daf9\'></a>\n\nThat such appraisal has been made in conformity with the appropriate State laws, Title VI of the 1964 Civil Rights Act, regulations and policies and procedures applicable to appraisal of right of way for such purposes; and that to the best of my knowledge no portion of the value assigned to such property consists of items which are non-compensable under the established law of said State.\n\n<a id=\'8cb8ca55-bc2e-4847-a951-63ad575987cd\'></a>\n\nThat neither my employment nor my compensation for making this appraisal and report are in any way contingent upon the values reported herein.\n\n<a id=\'383d4b77-cb9f-4cf2-ba98-1383ae415602\'></a>\n\nThat I have no direct or indirect present or contemplated future personal interest in such property or in any benefit from the acquisition of such property appraised.\n\n<a id=\'08e45352-f2b3-42f4-a39a-851af73e5158\'></a>\n\nThat I have not revealed the findings and results of such appraisal to anyone other than the proper officials of the California Department of Transportation or officials of the Federal Highway Administration and I will not do so until so authorized by State officials, or until I am required to do so by due process of law, or until I am released from this obligation by having publicly testified as to such findings.\n\n<a id=\'3485adcb-2b5f-406f-897d-78a35ed0a660\'></a>\n\nThat my opinion of the total fair market value of Parcel 36668-1, August 22nd, 2016 is $34,600.00, and that such conclusion was derived without collusion, coercion or direction as to value.\n\n<a id=\'1b35b71a-1327-479a-810b-efd7e045766f\'></a>\n\n<::attestation: Signature\nSigned\nSignature: legible\nout collusion, coercion or direction as to\nBlake Starr\nRight of Way Agent\nDate: 08/23/16\nA blue handwritten signature appears above the printed name "Blake Starr" and title "Right of Way Agent", with a handwritten date "08/23/16" below. Coughlan, also known as Laura Kathleen Coughlan, Successor Trustee of the Dennis E. Coughlan Revocable Trust, dated April 29, 1997, and Kimberly A. Coughlan Successor Trustee of the Mary Joan Cambell Revocable Trust, dated May 29, 1998\n\n<a id=\'dd3037e2-f757-4e19-9caf-304bad435b86\'></a>\n\nProperty Address: 006-280-046\nLocale: Smartsville\n\nZone: Rural Residential\nPresent Use: Rural Residential\nBest Use: Rural Residential\n\nEntire Property: Land: N/A\nImps: N/A\nTotal: N/A\n\nPossible Hazardous Waste (Include underground tanks)\noption Yes: [ ]\noption No: [x]\n\nDate Acquired: Over 5 years\nDTT: N/A\nConsideration: N/A\n\nTotal Property Area: 17± acres\noption Full: [ ]\nPart\noption Part: [x] (Include Access Rights)\noption Yes: [ ]\noption No: [x]\n\n<a id=\'450b53db-b4b9-417f-bc9a-fd8ea8e19b33\'></a>\n\nMarket Value of Required Property: $34,600.00 (Rounded)\nTotal: $34,560.17\n\nLand:\nIn R/W\n36668-1 (Fee Acquisition):\n72,851 SF x $0.33/SF $ 24,040.83\n\n49,068 SF Underlying Fee @ $1.00 $ 1.00\n\nImprovements:\nFencing $ 4,466.34\n(See "Improvements" section)\n\nDamages Less Benefits:\n(See "Remainder - Damages & Benefits" section) $ 6,052.00\n\n<a id=\'b46dff7f-78da-46f4-8cb9-88b53396aad5\'></a>\n\n**Construction Contract Work:**\nNone.\n\n**Total**                                                                 $ 34,560.17\n\nDate Inspected: 08/22/2016                                                  By: Blake Starr,\n                                                                           Right of Way Agent\n\n<a id=\'0f6a52a1-97f0-4726-ba4a-df13b49e6886\'></a>\n\n9\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'8db0a0fe-e01f-4641-846a-4eb2647287e0\'></a>\n\n# INTRODUCTION\nThis appraisal report contains the fair market valuation of one partial fee acquisition and one underlying fee acquisition that is needed in conjunction with this State Route 20 (SR20) Project. The partial acquisition is identified as Parcel 36668-1 on Caltrans Right of Way Appraisal Map A-2F590-03. The property, identified as APN 006-280-046, is vested to Laura & Kimberly Coughlan, trustees, in FEE SIMPLE interest, per the Placer Title Company Report dated December 31, 2015. The subject parcel is located along the eastbound lane of SR20, within the community of Smartsville and is vacant except for fencing that lies along the borders of the parcel.\n\n<a id=\'aed8e71e-586b-4199-a958-1735ab3c1c44\'></a>\n\nThe parcel identified as 36668 on the Caltrans Right of Way Map is approximately 123.8 acres.\nHowever, the property is split by a road separating approximately 17± acres of land from the remaining 106.8\nacres. This 17± acres contains the acquisition area, and it will be appraised as the larger parcel for the purpose\nof this appraisal and be referred to as the subject parcel. This is because the two parts of APN 006-280-043 share\nlittle utility together by being separated by a major road, can be separated legally with a lot-line adjustment, and\nwould be consistent with both the market trends and the parcels highest and best use.\n\n<a id=\'affb626e-72c0-4f9a-8e8f-84b004a59450\'></a>\n\n## AREA DESCRIPTION\n\nThe subject property is located in Yuba County along SR20 in the Sierra Nevada foothills and mountains near Smartsville, California. It is centrally located about 60 miles northeast of Sacramento, 91 miles west of Reno and 157 miles east of San Francisco. The cities of Grass Valley, Nevada City, Truckee and the unincorporated community of Penn Valley are the commercial hubs of the area.\n\n<a id=\'9dffc5a3-3399-496f-b318-988651944cf5\'></a>\n\nAccording to the U.S. Census Bureau, Yuba County has a total area of 644 square miles, of which 632 square miles is land and 12 square miles or 1.9% is water. It is the fifth-smallest county in California by total area. The county lies along the western slope of the Sierra Nevada, the steep slopes making it prime territory for the siting of hydroelectric power plants. A portion of the county, where Marysville (the county seat) and most of the population lives, is west of the mountains on the valley floor. There is a great deal of agriculture business in this part of the county, especially fruit orchards, rice fields, and cattle grazing. As of the 2010 census, the population was 72,155. The 2014 median household income was $45,470, the per capita income was $19,586 and there was a 21.6% poverty rate. Major highways that run through Yuba County are State Route 20, State Route 49, State Route 65 and State Route 70. Smartsville is located in Yuba County. As of the 2010 census, the population of Yuba County was 72,155. The county seat is Marysville. Major highways that run through Yuba County are State Route 20, State Route 49, State Route 65 and State Route 70.\n\n<a id=\'a0229210-b623-46aa-a2a4-bd77fad10cac\'></a>\n\n10\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'bdc0cbe5-355f-4a0e-a791-e4f13ef9ffe2\'></a>\n\nNEIGHBORHOOD DESCRIPTION\n\nThesubject property is located near the small unincorporated town of Smartsville. This area consists of mainly rural residential properties with some larger parcels used for agriculture. The subject\'s surrounding area was a small pioneer town where hydraulic or placer mining was practiced. Extensive placer mining tailings remain throughout the area. This area on Highway 20 is less than 0.2 mile southeast of the small commercial district and post office.\n\n<a id=\'f980766c-625e-4fbb-8d23-abbbafd6e790\'></a>\n\nThe subject property is located in an area of rural residential parcels, and it is accessed from Hammonton-Smartsville Road. The parcel is bordered by Highway 20 to the north with other rural residential parcels to the west, south, and north.\n\n<a id=\'905e4138-0bef-453f-b4fe-3e0754a4cbc7\'></a>\n\n## PARCEL DESCRIPTION\nThe subject property is located on Hammonton-Smartsville Road and State Route 20, near the town of Smartsville, and it is a part of the assessor\'s parcel number (APN) 006-280-046. This APN is roughly 123.80 acres in total, but roughly 17 acres is separated from the rest of the parcel by Hammonton-Smartsville Road. This 17± acres is considered to be the subject parcel for the purpose of this appraisal and will be identified as such. According to the Placer Title Company Title Report, dated December 31, 2015, title interest is vested to Laura & Kimberly Coughlan, and the interest in the land is FEE SIMPLE. According to Landvision®, the subject property is 17± acres, or 740,520 square feet, in size and is irregular in shape. The northern edge of the subject parcel borders SR20 and is full of shrubbery natural to the area. It is enclosed with fencing around all edges of the property. The subject parcel is improved with multiple fences (5 strand barbed-wire, 4 strand barbed-wire, and wire mesh fencing with 2 strand barbed-wire) along the north edge of the parcel, but for the purpose of this appraisal wire mesh with 2 strand barbed-wire will be used for replacement cost. There is also 5 strand barbed-wire fencing that is shared with the neighboring parcels.\n\n<a id=\'d859db37-706c-4663-b203-7d83425e9617\'></a>\n\n11\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'623c0ba2-660a-4ff8-87d7-83446a8ff8f4\'></a>\n\nCONSTRUCTION IN THE MANNER PROPOSED\n\nSR20, within the project limits, is a rural two-lane conventional highway, and currently has shoulder widths varying from 3 to 0 feet wide. It contains curves that provide poor line of sight when driving through it, and it does not experience any congestion. The current stretch of highway does not experience any winter flooding, but it does have a NID irrigation ditch running under it in several locations. The project will begin in Yuba County from 0.1 mile east of Smartsville Road at PM 20.1, and it will end at Mooney Flat Road at PM 0.1 in Nevada County.\n\n<a id=\'0be247f8-4602-4962-8dcd-85e8069b8ae6\'></a>\n\nAs a result of its poor visibility around curves and limited shoulders, this section of SR20 has been experiencing more accidents than average. To remedy this, Caltrans is:\n\n<a id=\'8accbeb5-549e-4a7e-8ce6-60952693981e\'></a>\n\n- Realigning curves to provide two 1,000 foot radius reverse curves and a single 1,000 foot radius broken back curve.\n- Widening the road to provide 12 foot wide lanes.\n- Extending shoulder width to 8 feet.\n- Improving superelevation and superelevation transitions.\n- Increasing line of sight distance.\n- Adding turn pockets.\n- Improve profiling.\n- Upgrading drainage facilities.\n- Cold plane and overlay at both ends of the project.\n\n<a id=\'551d2843-21a9-4444-8bd4-fdea7f7ccdc6\'></a>\n\nAt the subject parcel\'s location, the acquisition will be used to realign SR20 to the new 1,000 foot radius curve, widen the lanes to current highway standards, and allow for a 4:1 slope along the highway\'s\n\n<a id=\'cd59bf94-bd73-4c45-9fb6-32bc2dad3cc2\'></a>\n\n**HIGHEST AND BEST USE**\n\n"Highest and Best Use" is defined in the *Appraisal of Real Estate, 12th Edition, AIREA 2001* as:\n\n"*The reasonably probable and legal use of vacant land or an improved property, that is physically possible, appropriately supported, and financially feasible and that results in the highest value*".\n\n<a id=\'06d7df18-194f-4dad-895f-ecc34de28c34\'></a>\n\nThe following tests must be met in estimating the highest and best use. The use must be legal; the use\nmust be probable, not speculative or conjectural. There must be a profitable demand for such use and it must\n\n<a id=\'20fd54b4-006a-4bb3-84fd-d56609156b11\'></a>\n\n12\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'15f70b64-45c5-406b-b61f-3199c7f2756d\'></a>\n\nreturn to the land the highest net return for the longest period of time.\n\n*   Legally Permissible Use – What uses are permitted legally under existing zoning, building codes, environmental regulations, and public/private deed restrictions?\n*   Physically Possible Use – What uses of the site are physically possible, given its size, shape, area, terrain, soils, ingress/egress, and assembly potential?\n*   Financially Feasible Use – Which possible and permissible uses will produce a positive net return to the owner of the property?\n*   Maximally Productive Use – Considering all feasible uses, which use will produce the highest residual land value consistent with the rate of return warranted by the market for that use?\n\n<a id=\'c8bfb54d-ce29-43c6-9ef0-7461f497b32a\'></a>\n\n## Legal Permissibility\n\nThe zoning of this parcel is Rural Residential Five Acre (RR-5) by the Yuba County Planning Department. This zoning allows for a density of one residential unit per five acres within the required setbacks and other criteria. The subject area is 17± acres and will support one single-family residence on the parcel as it exists now, per the Yuba County zoning designation as a **legally permissible** use. The parcel can also be subdivided into 3 smaller 5 acre lots, per the Yuba County Planning. Agricultural uses are also permitted within the RR-5 zoning ordinance. This eliminates any commercial, industrial or other uses on the subject property.\n\n<a id=\'34815a61-59df-4461-9495-938fe2470d86\'></a>\n\n## Physically Possible\n\nThe subject site is typical in size compared to the surrounding parcels with level topography. The size and shape of the parcel are functional and would **physically** allow for most types of residential structures, and small agricultural uses.\n\n<a id=\'a1cff982-7c5c-4d6d-93e9-c9913440ba56\'></a>\n\nFinancially Feasible\nThe determination of financial feasibility is based primarily on demand. The subject is located near recent land divisions for residential use. There is also ample agricultural activity in the region. Therefore, it would be financially feasible to obtain this parcel for a residential home, or agricultural site.\n\n<a id=\'bdfa8a8e-7725-4f24-ab17-916da36aeaa0\'></a>\n\n13\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'36060946-37d2-498a-8bfd-f48f082c120a\'></a>\n\nMaximally Productive\nAfter evaluation of the legally permissible, physically possible, and financially feasible uses, the maximally productive use of the subject property is as Rural Residential Five Acres, with the primary use as a home site.\n\n<a id=\'0f02e5d9-0162-48a6-8ca9-2c616672bf1a\'></a>\n\nHIGHEST AND BEST USE CONCLUSION – AS THOUGH VACANT\n\n<a id=\'da6df6b6-dc76-4729-bd0d-838bd9e1291e\'></a>\n\nThe appraiser has performed the four tests of highest and best use as though vacant. The conclusion of highest and best use as vacant is Rural Residential.\n\n<a id=\'1e62d760-ede3-4e0e-84cc-6137a642b1b4\'></a>\n\n## METHODOLOGY\n\n### Sales Comparison for Land Value\n\nThere are six land valuation techniques recognized by the Appraisal Institute. These are sales comparison, allocation, extraction, subdivision development, land residual, and ground rent capitalization. The sales comparison approach is the most common and preferred method when sufficient market data is available. The appraiser has sufficient comparable market data, and therefore will rely solely on the sales comparison approach in deriving a unit value. This involves analyzing and comparing the sales of comparable properties, then adjusting them to the subject property to estimate value.\n\n<a id=\'4e8ebd47-ee2d-49a5-8149-852f99789e58\'></a>\n\n## LAND VALUATION\n\nIn determining the site value, vacant land sales used in valuing the subject encompassed the city of Smartsville and surrounding areas. Sources used were the Yuba County Assessor\'s files, Landvision® and interviews with real estate agents in the area.\n\n<a id=\'28a12590-b788-45eb-9b5c-4bec00e56a88\'></a>\n\nAll sales used were cash or cash equivalent sales; therefore no finance adjustments were necessary. The listing also offered no special financing. The market data used in this section sold from August 2014 to the current listing. Discussions with the Assessor\'s office and other brokers in the area indicate there has not been a significant change in rural residential property values over this period, therefore no adjustments for market conditions were made to the first 3 comparables. The comparables used have the same zoning as the subject and have similar utility as the subject property. All comparables used were also located in areas of custom homes with views of the surrounding mountains or valleys. All sites have been perc/mantle tested for septic, and included power on site. These comparables were chosen mainly based on size and location, and will be discussed below and analyzed on the spreadsheet on the opposite page.\n\n<a id=\'caec08b3-4cc9-48ba-8ca6-5f90c5011643\'></a>\n\n14\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'b03a5136-e7c5-4a04-8585-ba022f1cba7f\'></a>\n\nCOMPARABLE SALES DATA GRID\n\n<a id=\'1644ea91-40c0-4fa7-a2a9-bad23547f567\'></a>\n\n15\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'5d93b0ed-dd68-4039-84fd-5d4ccffd0bab\'></a>\n\n## DISCUSSION OF ADJUSTMENTS FOR SALES COMPARISON APPROACH\n\nAfter speaking with brokers, realtors, and the Yuba County Tax Assessor\'s office about the values added by different property characteristics in the Smartsville area, it was concluded that access to the NID irrigation ditch adds 15% to a property\'s value, a capped-well with no electrical or pump adds $6,000.00, and a completed perc/mantle test adds $5,000.00. After an analysis of listed and actual sale price in the Smartsville area, a 5% reduction in listing prices was deemed reasonable to adjust listings to market value. Through an analysis of available comparables, and interviews with sellers, a 10% adjustment is necessary to reflect the decreased value of properties that have their only access through a road easement over another parcel.\n\n<a id=\'d9af9384-4deb-4564-acdc-c64d8382b693\'></a>\n\nComparable 1 is an August 2014 sale of a vacant 19.63 acre parcel located west of the subject, in the community of Smartsville. According to the Yuba County Planning Department, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. Access is via McGanney Lane. Electric and telephone are to the site. There is a domestic well on site and it has two approved septic areas. It has rights to the NID for irrigation purposes but currently does not draw from the ditch. This was a private sale with seller financing; no broker was involved. According to the sellers, the transaction is considered an arm\'s length transaction and reflective of the market. A downward adjustment of $10,000.00 was made to Comparable 1 to reflect the added value the perc/mantles contributed to the comparable and a downward adjustment of $6,000.00 was made to reflect the added value of the capped-well. After all the adjustments were applied, the site\'s raw land value is $243,000.00.\n\n<a id=\'ee0e0578-7712-4419-9817-7f2d69a32e4e\'></a>\n\nComparable 2 is an August 2014 sale of a vacant 20.32-acre parcel located northwest of the subject property, across SR20, in the community of Smartsville. According to the Yuba County Planning Department, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. Access is via a road easement to McGanney Lane. Electric and telephone are to the site. The site does not have a domestic well but does have one approved septic area. It has rights to the Nevada Irrigation Ditch (NID) for irrigation purposes but currently does not draw from the ditch. This was a private sale with seller financing; no broker was involved. According to the sellers, the transaction is considered an arm\'s length transaction and reflective of the market. The sale price included $62,600.00 paid by the buyer to improve McGanney Lane and install a fire suppression pond for the seller to allow the 80 acres to be subdivided by Yuba County requirements; this is reflected in the "Adjustement for Expenditure as Condition of Escrow". A downward adjustment of $5,000.00 was made to Comparable 2 to reflect the added value the perc/mantle contributed to the comparable. An upwards adjustment of 10% was made to the properties access for having access only through a road easement from another parcel. After all the adjustments were applied, the property\'s site value is approximately $242,100.00.\n\n<a id=\'460fe85b-2abc-441e-8353-bfa5ee824773\'></a>\n\nComparable 3 is an August 2014 sale of a vacant 20.00-acre parcel located 0.1 miles west of the subject in the community of Smartsville. According to the sellers, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. Access is via a road easement to McGanney Lane. Electric and telephone are to the site. The site has one domestic well and three approved septic areas. It has rights to the Nevada Irrigation Ditch (NID) for irrigation purposes but currently does not draw from the ditch. The sale price included $62,600.00 paid by the buyer to improve McGanney Lane and install a fire suppression pond for the seller to allow the 80 acres to be subdivided by Yuba County requirements; this is reflected in the "Adjustment for Expenditure as Condition of Escrow". A downward adjustment of $15,000.00 was made to Comparable 3 to reflect the added value the perc/mantles contributed to the comparable and a downwards adjustment of $6,000.00 was made to reflect the added value of the capped-well. An upwards adjustment of 10% was made to the parcel\'s access for having access only through a road easement from another parcel. After all the adjustments were applied, the property\'s site value is approximately $234,400.00.\n\n<a id=\'4398d33f-f2db-49d7-a457-d39931b7f0ca\'></a>\n\n16\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'858a0b3b-5220-4314-8ad4-03c29bb23a36\'></a>\n\nComparable 4 is a current listing of a vacant 20.42-acre parcel located 1.9 miles southwest of the subject within the Smartsville community boundary. According to the Yuba County Planning Department, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. The parcel has frontage along Hammonton-Smartsville Road and Seven Moons Lanes. Electric and telephone are to the site. The site has one domestic well and one approved septic area. The parcel resides outside the Nevada Irrigation Ditch (NID) service district, but the Railroad Commissions Act does allow access to NID water; however, due to the distance between the parcel and the NID irrigation ditch, this parcel is to be viewed as being unable to access the NID in a manner that makes economic sense being that the closest NID ditch is approximately 3,200 feet to the northeast across several other parcels. Through an analysis of surrounding area listing and sales prices, it was determined that a 5% reduction on the listing price was needed to normalize the listing price to reflect a market transaction. A downward adjustment of $5,000.00 was made to Comparable 4 to reflect the added value the perc/mantle contributed to the comparable and a downward adjustment of $6,000.00 to reflect the added value of the capped-well. An upwards adjustment of 15% was made to the property\'s value to reflect the inability to effectively hook-up to the NID irrigation ditch. After all the adjustments were applied, the property\'s site value is approximately $241,900.00.\n\n<a id=\'f44b48fb-c408-46a7-b5ef-611e2dc9b728\'></a>\n\nRECONCILIATION OF UNIT VALUE\n\nTheThe market data comparables were analyzed and resulted in a site range of $234,400.00 to $243,000.00 for the subject property. All comparables were weighted relatively equally against each other with an emphasis placed on comparable 1 because it required the least amount of adjustments of the comparables. Each were similar to the subject in respect to their utility, located in the immediate area of the subject property, and are representative of the current market. With the above analysis in mind, the appraiser has estimated the land value of the subject to be $243,000.00 as vacant.\n\n<a id=\'8c43701a-22e5-47ca-a07d-146575aa4b13\'></a>\n\n17\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'8beb4e2a-8409-47bb-a5e0-30ba12e18851\'></a>\n\nTHE ACQUISITION\n\n<a id=\'d659ee50-95fe-474d-bc05-f213bc17d0e7\'></a>\n\nThe State\'s acquisition consists of underlying fee under the current right of way and a fee parcel that runs along the northern edge of the subject adjacent to State Route 20. This fee parcel (Parcel 36668-1 on the R/W maps) consists of 72,851 SF of the parcel\'s northern border. This area is needed to accommodate the new SR20 alignment to lessen the severity of the curve at the subject\'s location, allow for a 4:1 slope along the highway, and extend the shoulders to 8\' wide. The fee acquisition will leave the parcel with a remainder of 667,669 SF, or 15.33 acres. The 40,826 SF of underlying fee area on State Route 20 (shown on the R/W maps) as Parcel 36668-1 is the State\'s existing right of way and is held in Highway easement. Since it is encumbered, and holds no utility to the property owner, it will be appraised at $1.00.\n\n<a id=\'bc75c946-c750-40ab-abfe-92dbeac82369\'></a>\n\nWith that said, a site value of $243,000.00 was determined in the previous section for the land value.\nFor calculating purposes, an overall square foot value will be used. The determination of the overall square\nfoot value is as follows:\n\n<a id=\'15eeb8cb-48c8-402a-afad-f4f89daf3b31\'></a>\n\n$243,000.00 ÷ 740,520 SF (site size) = $0.33/SF\n\n<a id=\'2b19905c-6e7b-41b6-8dbd-864b5dc19ce3\'></a>\n\n<table id="17-1">\n<tr><td id="17-2" colspan="2">Calculations for these parcels are as follows:</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-3">Parcel 36668-1 (Fee Acquisition)</td><td id="17-4"></td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-5">72,851 @ $0.33/SF</td><td id="17-6">= $24,040.83</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-7">Parcel 36668-1 (Underlying Fee)</td><td id="17-8"></td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-9">20,178 SF @ $1.00</td><td id="17-a">= $1.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-b">Total Land Value</td><td id="17-c">$24,041.83</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'c595ad64-31d1-4a97-8a46-41d07c212cae\'></a>\n\n18\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'c1fa739b-c957-4073-8682-9a869eca3fd5\'></a>\n\nIMPROVEMENTS\nThe improvements in the proposed acquisition area consist of approximately 1,040 linear feet of 4-strand-barbed-wire fence, 5 strand barbed-wire fence, and wire mesh fence with 2 strand barbed-wire. For the purpose of this appraisal, the highest price per unit of the 3 types was used to calculate, that being the wire mesh on steel posts with 2 strands of barbed-wire. To obtain a price for wire mesh fencing with 2 strand barbed-wire across the top in the Smartsville area, Action Fencing of Marysville was contacted. During conversations with the contractor, it was deemed that $8.00/LF was the cost for wire mesh fencing with 2 strand barbed-wire. During inspection of the property and the fencing, it was observed to be 50% depreciated, that is to say that 50% of its useful life is remaining. Approximately 197 LF of shared 5 strand barbed-wire fencing is to be acquired, and this value will be split between the two respective owners. During inspection of the property and the fencing, it was observed to be 50% depreciated, that is to say that 50% of its useful life is remaining.\n\n<a id=\'c65fbbde-5bad-4939-81ca-5ac50f96ce83\'></a>\n\n<table id="18-1">\n<tr><td id="18-2" colspan="2">Fencing Improvements</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-3" colspan="2">Fencing (wire mesh on steel posts)</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-4">- 1,040 LF x $8.00/LF</td><td id="18-5">$ 8,320.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-6">Depreciation (50% x $8,320.00)</td><td id="18-7">$ 4,160.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-8">Fencing Total</td><td id="18-9">$ 4,160.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-a" colspan="2">Fencing (shared barbed-wire)</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-b">-½ (197 LF x $6.22/LF)</td><td id="18-c">$ 612.67</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-d">Depreciation (50% x $612.67)</td><td id="18-e">$ 306.33</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-f">Fencing Total</td><td id="18-g">$ 306.34</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-h">Final Improvements Value</td><td id="18-i">$ 4,466.34</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'81e47563-ae2d-4df0-b903-eb439d8b4646\'></a>\n\n19\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'e47200f7-af98-4d77-af8a-89eac5131faf\'></a>\n\nREMAINDER – DAMAGES AND BENEFITS\n\n1 ... [illegible]\n\n<a id=\'1f98164d-3030-4037-8599-1ed37c152b97\'></a>\n\nThe costs per unit were explained, and calculated, in the improvements section were used for calculating the damages as well. Depreciation of the improvements, for the purpose of the calculation of damages, was explained, and used, in the Improvement section as well. Approximately 1,040 linear feet of the existing wire mesh fencing will need to be replaced to bring the parcel to the same utility as the before condition; this is calculated new at $8,320.00 ($8.00/LF X 1,040 LF). Of this amount, the depreciated value in place was already paid in the improvements section in the amount of $4,160.00 ($8,320.00 X 50%). The cost to cure was calculated as $4,160.00 ($8,320.00 X 50%). Due to the acquisition, an additional 70 LF of fencing will be required to be installed on the northern border to restore utility to the parcel. This was calculated with a replacement cost new of $560.00 ($8.00/LF X 70 LF).\n\n<a id=\'df15ff2b-dfc8-4592-bc8c-248c5e19b638\'></a>\n\nA contingency fee of 15% will be added to the replacement cost new (shown below) to account for\nany oversight by the grantor, or unforeseen labor or material costs.\n\n<a id=\'3dab9aea-ea22-4f3f-9646-942090b65a97\'></a>\n\n<table id="19-1">\n<tr><td Caltrans Design Engineer Kevin Lee, there is no Construction Contract work needed for this parcel.\n\n<a id=\'f4774eb9-bec1-4bd7-bcbe-b04e936f250f\'></a>\n\nSUMMARY OF THE BASIS FOR JUST COMPENSATION\n\nThe sales comparison approach was used to determine land value due to comparable sale availability and similarity to the subject. The cost approach was used to determine the replacement cost of the fencing improvements that fell in the acquisition area. Costs were obtained from The Marshall & Swift (M&S) Residential Cost Handbook, and estimates from local contractors. Curable damages were valued by the replacement cost of a new fence minus the improvements\' depreciated value in place. No incurable damages will be sustained from the partial acquisition as the remainder will not lose any utility. No special benefits were noted as a result of the proposed project.\n\n<a id=\'6dadee37-1930-4b70-874b-acb73609abc4\'></a>\n\n21\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'d95a4ab4-9f3c-419e-aee0-7ef13b1eaef8\'></a>\n\n# APPENDIX\n* Comparable Data Summary Page\n* Comparable Data Map\n* Comparable Data Sheets\n* Comparable Tax Assessor Maps\n* Appraisal Terms (3 pgs.)\n* R/W Engineering Appraisal Map (1 pg.)\n\n<a id=\'e015bd11-2a18-4768-9d42-3d8586458e70\'></a>\n\n22\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'f94c0bd1-3ea0-4887-9a9d-915bb10b4621\'></a>\n\nCOMPARABLE SUMMARY PAGE\n\n<a id=\'fb5be767-9b1c-40ac-828c-519112b4597f\'></a>\n\n<table id="22-1">\n<tr><td id="22-2">Comp No.</td><td id="22-3">C.O.E.</td><td id="22-4">Location</td><td id="22-5">Price</td><td id="22-6">Site Size</td><td id="22-7">Price Per Site</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-8">1</td><td id="22-9">08/03/14</td><td id="22-a">McGanney Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-b">$ 259,000.00</td><td id="22-c">19.63 Acres</td><td id="22-d">$ 259,000.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-e">2</td><td id="22-f">08/03/14</td><td id="22-g">McGanney Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-h">$ 225,100.00</td><td id="22-i">20.32 Acres</td><td id="22-j">$ 225,100.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-k">3</td><td id="22-l">08/11/14</td><td id="22-m">McGanney Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-n">$ 234,100.00</td><td id="22-o">20.00 Acres</td><td id="22-p">$ 234,100.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-q">4</td><td id="22-r">Listing</td><td id="22-s">Seven Moons Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-t">$ 233,000.00</td><td id="22-u">20.42 Acres</td><td id="22-v">$ 233,000.00</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'edb979ab-61a1-4d7a-9b8b-d5884cbf72b3\'></a>\n\n23\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'9a5b16b2-8466-48b0-875f-8f093ae5fe6f\'></a>\n\nCOMPARABLE MAP SHEET\n\n<a id=\'02ac30b9-b890-43c5-873b-30dcbae75a0e\'></a>\n\n<::Aerial map showing properties and comparable listings. [California Code of Civil Procedure §1263.430]\n\n<a id=\'08a7ecbf-f2fb-4f35-b394-0bf0348fdaf5\'></a>\n\nComparable Sales\nWhen relevant to the determination of the value of property, a witness may take into account as a basis for his opinion the price and other terms and circumstances of any sale or contract to sell and purchase comparable property if the sale or contract was freely made in good faith within a reasonable time before or after the date of valuation. In order to be considered comparable, the sale or contract must have been made sufficiently near in time to the date of valuation, and the property sold must be located sufficiently near the property being valued, and must be sufficiently alike in respect to character, size, situation, usability, and improvements, to make it clear that the property sold and the property being valued are comparable in value and that the price realized for the property sold may fairly be considered as shedding light on the value of the property being valued. [California Evidence Code §816]\n\n<a id=\'82a9b50f-b10d-4fba-bae7-75e34f55c710\'></a>\n\n**Damage to Remainder**\nDamage to the remainder is the damage, if any, caused to the remainder by either or both of the following:\n\n(a) The severance of the remainder from the part taken.\n\n(b) The construction and use of the project for which the property is taken in the manner proposed by the plaintiff whether or not the damage is caused by a portion of the project located on the part taken.\n[California Code of Civil Procedure §1263.420]\n\n<a id=\'1456e2e1-2d92-4743-b7c0-c8982f0679a2\'></a>\n\n**Easement**\nAn interest in real property that conveys use, but not ownership, of a portion of an owner\'s property. Access or right of way easements may be acquired by private parties or public utilities. Governments dedicate conservation, open space, and preservation easements. [The Dictionary of Real Estate Appraisal, 5th ed. Appraisal Institute; Defined: Civil Code § 801 et seq.]\n\n<a id=\'b1a1de79-8e0e-4c62-9de2-a0f2dcdfe4ac\'></a>\n\n**Fair Market Value**\n(a) The fair market value of the property taken is the highest price on the date of valuation that would be agreed to by a seller, being willing to sell but under no particular or urgent necessity for so doing, nor obliged to sell, and a buyer, being ready, willing, and able to buy but under no particular necessity for doing so, each dealing with the other with full knowledge of all the uses and purposes for which the property is reasonably adaptable and available.\n\n<a id=\'65e2e07f-dca6-4e8f-9f95-f15ab41ed04e\'></a>\n\n(b) The fair market value of property taken for which there is no relevant, comparable market is its value on the date of valuation as determined by any method of valuation that is just and equitable. [California Code of Civil Procedure Section 1263.320]\n\n<a id=\'c82a5793-51c0-4366-a920-b85c7b0aaba1\'></a>\n\n33\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'fb9a1089-0bfd-4e68-a5d8-c879f5694c06\'></a>\n\nFee Simple\nAbsolute ownership unencumbered by any other interest or estate, subject only to the limitations imposed by the governmental powers of taxation, eminent domain, police powers and escheat. [The Dictionary of Real Estate Appraisal, 5th ed. Appraisal Institute]\n\n<a id=\'3008d757-90c6-4215-80aa-122e3339d4bf\'></a>\n\nHighest and Best Use\nThe reasonably probable and legal use of vacant land or an improved property, which is physically possible, appropriately supported, financially feasible, and that results in the highest value. The four criteria the highest and best use must meet are legal permissibility, physical possibility, financial feasibility, and maximum productivity. [The Dictionary of Real Estate Appraisal, 5th Edition - Appraisal Institute]\n\n<a id=\'03a38910-14c7-4899-ba59-70ae57339c4f\'></a>\n\nImprovements Pertaining to the Realty\n\n(a) "Improvements pertaining to the realty" include any machinery or equipment installed for use on property taken by eminent domain, or on the remainder if such property is part of a larger parcel that cannot be removed without a substantial economic loss or without substantial damage to the property on which it is installed, regardless of the method of installation.\n\n(b) In determining whether particular property can be removed "without substantial economic loss" within the meaning of this section, the value of property in place considered as a part of the realty should be compared with its value if it were removed and sold. [California Code of Civil Procedure 1263.205]\n\n<a id=\'a18a9649-7001-43e1-99b8-e7022b3d9db8\'></a>\n\n**Larger Parcel**\n"The tract or tracts of land which are under the beneficial control of a single individual or entity and have the same, or an integrated, highest and best use. Elements for consideration by the appraiser in making a determination in this regard are contiguity, or proximity, as it bears on the highest and best use of the property, unity of ownership, and unity of highest and best use".\nUnity of ownership, contiguity, and unity of use, the three conditions that establish the larger parcel for the consideration of severance damages." [The Dictionary of Real Estate Appraisal, 5th Edition - Appraisal Institute]\n\n<a id=\'a20bedc7-871c-4da0-affd-d758fbafca6f\'></a>\n\n**Personal Information**\nThe term "personal information" means any information that is maintained by an agency that identifies or describes an individual, including, but not limited to, his or her name, social security number, physical description, home address, home telephone number, education, financial matters, and medical or employment history. It includes statements made by, or attributed to, the individual. [California Civil Code §1798.3]\n\n<a id=\'21ac9f80-1889-4e48-92e6-c38935a8c316\'></a>\n\nRemainder\n"In eminent domain condemnation, that portion of a larger parcel remaining in the ownership of the property owner after a partial taking." [The Dictionary of Real Estate Appraisal, 5th ed. Appraisal Institute]\n\n<a id=\'afcc1181-caaa-4ff7-93d6-2fa736b3406f\'></a>\n\n34\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'5d5ac9be-eda5-44e8-bf44-bff70c0e69bc\'></a>\n\nTemporary Construction Easement\nProvides work area for the temporary use of land outside normal right of way that is necessary for construction of the project. The use of this land will be for a specified time period and the purpose of the TCE must be clearly shown on the plans.\n\n<a id=\'6eb88285-f99a-44de-ab7f-21b505e1fcfc\'></a>\n\nUnit Rule or Undivided Fee Rule\nThe unit rule has two aspects; one relating to the interests, or estates, into which ownership of real estate may be carved, and the second relating to the various physical components of real estate.\n\n<a id=\'c63d7405-8dc4-43ab-b346-8177c8783f3a\'></a>\n\nThe first aspect of the unit rule requires that property be valued as a whole rather than by the sum of the values of the various interests into which it may have been carved, such as lessor and lessee, life tenant and remainder man, and mortgagor and mortgagee, etc. This is an application of the principle that it is the property, not the various interests, that is being acquired. Appurtenant easements and similar use restrictions create an exception to this aspect of the unit rule. When lands are encumbered by such an appurtenant easement, they are valued as encumbered.\n\n<a id=\'a78ff02d-df88-4a03-8864-5333636dc089\'></a>\n\nA second aspect of the unit rule is that different elements or components of a tract of land are not to be separately valued and added together. Such a procedure results in a summation or cumulative appraisal, which is forbidden in appraisals for federal acquisitions, as it is in general real estate appraisal practice.\n[Uniform Appraisal Standards for Federal Land Acquisitions 2000]\n\n<a id=\'644f91bc-e260-4907-bb88-f4f5ceeebc2f\'></a>\n\n35\n\n<!-- PAGE BREAK -->\n\n<a id=\'13f57e60-9d1e-45f9-bcc9-06403beba1de\'></a>\n\nCOUNTY OF YUBA\\nT16N, R6E, MDM\\nSECTIONS 33 & 34\\n\\nNOTE: The State of California or its officers or agents\\nshall not be responsible for the accuracy or\\ncompleteness of digital images of this map.\\n\\n<::map\\n: A survey map overlaid on an aerial image showing land parcels, roads, and various easements. Coughlan Successor Trustee of the Mary Joan Cambell Revocable Trust, dated May 29, 1998\n\n<a id=\'dd3037e2-f757-4e19-9caf-304bad435b86\'></a>\n\nProperty Address: 006-280-046\nLocale: Smartsville\n\nZone: Rural Residential\nPresent Use: Rural Residential\nBest Use: Rural Residential\n\nEntire Property: Land: N/A\nImps: N/A\nTotal: N/A\n\nPossible Hazardous Waste (Include underground tanks)\noption Yes: [ ]\noption No: [x]\n\nDate Acquired: Over 5 years\nDTT: N/A\nConsideration: N/A\n\nTotal Property Area: 17± acres\noption Full: [ ]\nPart\noption Part: [x] (Include Access Rights)\noption Yes: [ ]\noption No: [x]\n\n<a id=\'450b53db-b4b9-417f-bc9a-fd8ea8e19b33\'></a>\n\nMarket Value of Required Property: $34,600.00 (Rounded)\nTotal: $34,560.17\n\nLand:\nIn R/W\n36668-1 (Fee Acquisition):\n72,851 SF x $0.33/SF $ 24,040.83\n\n49,068 SF Underlying Fee @ $1.00 $ 1.00\n\nImprovements:\nFencing $ 4,466.34\n(See "Improvements" section)\n\nDamages Less Benefits:\n(See "Remainder - Damages & Benefits" section) $ 6,052.00\n\n<a id=\'b46dff7f-78da-46f4-8cb9-88b53396aad5\'></a>\n\n**Construction Contract Work:**\nNone.\n\n**Total**                                                                 $ 34,560.17\n\nDate Inspected: 08/22/2016                                                  By: Blake Starr,\n                                                                           Right of Way Agent\n\n<a id=\'0f6a52a1-97f0-4726-ba4a-df13b49e6886\'></a>\n\n9\n\n<a id=\'8db0a0fe-e01f-4641-846a-4eb2647287e0\'></a>\n\n# INTRODUCTION\nThis appraisal report contains the fair market valuation of one partial fee acquisition and one underlying fee acquisition that is needed in conjunction with this State Route 20 (SR20) Project. The partial acquisition is identified as Parcel 36668-1 on Caltrans Right of Way Appraisal Map A-2F590-03. The property, identified as APN 006-280-046, is vested to Laura & Kimberly Coughlan, trustees, in FEE SIMPLE interest, per the Placer Title Company Report dated December 31, 2015. The subject parcel is located along the eastbound lane of SR20, within the community of Smartsville and is vacant except for fencing that lies along the borders of the parcel.\n\n<a id=\'aed8e71e-586b-4199-a958-1735ab3c1c44\'></a>\n\nThe parcel identified as 36668 on the Caltrans Right of Way Map is approximately 123.8 acres.\nHowever, the property is split by a road separating approximately 17± acres of land from the remaining 106.8\nacres. This 17± acres contains the acquisition area, and it will be appraised as the larger parcel for the purpose\nof this appraisal and be referred to as the subject parcel. This is because the two parts of APN 006-280-043 share\nlittle utility together by being separated by a major road, can be separated legally with a lot-line adjustment, and\nwould be consistent with both the market trends and the parcels highest and best use.\n\n<a id=\'affb626e-72c0-4f9a-8e8f-84b004a59450\'></a>\n\n## AREA DESCRIPTION\n\nThe subject property is located in Yuba County along SR20 in the Sierra Nevada foothills and mountains near Smartsville, California. It is centrally located about 60 miles northeast of Sacramento, 91 miles west of Reno and 157 miles east of San Francisco. The cities of Grass Valley, Nevada City, Truckee and the unincorporated community of Penn Valley are the commercial hubs of the area.\n\n<a id=\'9dffc5a3-3399-496f-b318-988651944cf5\'></a>\n\nAccording to the U.S. Census Bureau, Yuba County has a total area of 644 square miles, of which 632 square miles is land and 12 square miles or 1.9% is water. It is the fifth-smallest county in California by total area. The county lies along the western slope of the Sierra Nevada, the steep slopes making it prime territory for the siting of hydroelectric power plants. A portion of the county, where Marysville (the county seat) and most of the population lives, is west of the mountains on the valley floor. There is a great deal of agriculture business in this part of the county, especially fruit orchards, rice fields, and cattle grazing. As of the 2010 census, the population was 72,155. The 2014 median household income was $45,470, the per capita income was $19,586 and there was a 21.6% poverty rate. Major highways that run through Yuba County are State Route 20, State Route 49, State Route 65 and State Route 70. Smartsville is located in Yuba County. As of the 2010 census, the population of Yuba County was 72,155. The county seat is Marysville. Major highways that run through Yuba County are State Route 20, State Route 49, State Route 65 and State Route 70.\n\n<a id=\'a0229210-b623-46aa-a2a4-bd77fad10cac\'></a>\n\n10\n\n<a id=\'bdc0cbe5-355f-4a0e-a791-e4f13ef9ffe2\'></a>\n\nNEIGHBORHOOD DESCRIPTION\n\nThesubject property is located near the small unincorporated town of Smartsville. This area consists of mainly rural residential properties with some larger parcels used for agriculture. The subject\'s surrounding area was a small pioneer town where hydraulic or placer mining was practiced. Extensive placer mining tailings remain throughout the area. This area on Highway 20 is less than 0.2 mile southeast of the small commercial district and post office.\n\n<a id=\'f980766c-625e-4fbb-8d23-abbbafd6e790\'></a>\n\nThe subject property is located in an area of rural residential parcels, and it is accessed from Hammonton-Smartsville Road. The parcel is bordered by Highway 20 to the north with other rural residential parcels to the west, south, and north.\n\n<a id=\'905e4138-0bef-453f-b4fe-3e0754a4cbc7\'></a>\n\n## PARCEL DESCRIPTION\nThe subject property is located on Hammonton-Smartsville Road and State Route 20, near the town of Smartsville, and it is a part of the assessor\'s parcel number (APN) 006-280-046. This APN is roughly 123.80 acres in total, but roughly 17 acres is separated from the rest of the parcel by Hammonton-Smartsville Road. This 17± acres is considered to be the subject parcel for the purpose of this appraisal and will be identified as such. According to the Placer Title Company Title Report, dated December 31, 2015, title interest is vested to Laura & Kimberly Coughlan, and the interest in the land is FEE SIMPLE. According to Landvision®, the subject property is 17± acres, or 740,520 square feet, in size and is irregular in shape. The northern edge of the subject parcel borders SR20 and is full of shrubbery natural to the area. It is enclosed with fencing around all edges of the property. The subject parcel is improved with multiple fences (5 strand barbed-wire, 4 strand barbed-wire, and wire mesh fencing with 2 strand barbed-wire) along the north edge of the parcel, but for the purpose of this appraisal wire mesh with 2 strand barbed-wire will be used for replacement cost. There is also 5 strand barbed-wire fencing that is shared with the neighboring parcels.\n\n<a id=\'d859db37-706c-4663-b203-7d83425e9617\'></a>\n\n11\n\n<a id=\'623c0ba2-660a-4ff8-87d7-83446a8ff8f4\'></a>\n\nCONSTRUCTION IN THE MANNER PROPOSED\n\nSR20, within the project limits, is a rural two-lane conventional highway, and currently has shoulder widths varying from 3 to 0 feet wide. It contains curves that provide poor line of sight when driving through it, and it does not experience any congestion. The current stretch of highway does not experience any winter flooding, but it does have a NID irrigation ditch running under it in several locations. The project will begin in Yuba County from 0.1 mile east of Smartsville Road at PM 20.1, and it will end at Mooney Flat Road at PM 0.1 in Nevada County.\n\n<a id=\'0be247f8-4602-4962-8dcd-85e8069b8ae6\'></a>\n\nAs a result of its poor visibility around curves and limited shoulders, this section of SR20 has been experiencing more accidents than average. To remedy this, Caltrans is:\n\n<a id=\'8accbeb5-549e-4a7e-8ce6-60952693981e\'></a>\n\n- Realigning curves to provide two 1,000 foot radius reverse curves and a single 1,000 foot radius broken back curve.\n- Widening the road to provide 12 foot wide lanes.\n- Extending shoulder width to 8 feet.\n- Improving superelevation and superelevation transitions.\n- Increasing line of sight distance.\n- Adding turn pockets.\n- Improve profiling.\n- Upgrading drainage facilities.\n- Cold plane and overlay at both ends of the project.\n\n<a id=\'551d2843-21a9-4444-8bd4-fdea7f7ccdc6\'></a>\n\nAt the subject parcel\'s location, the acquisition will be used to realign SR20 to the new 1,000 foot radius curve, widen the lanes to current highway standards, and allow for a 4:1 slope along the highway\'s\n\n<a id=\'cd59bf94-bd73-4c45-9fb6-32bc2dad3cc2\'></a>\n\n**HIGHEST AND BEST USE**\n\n"Highest and Best Use" is defined in the *Appraisal of Real Estate, 12th Edition, AIREA 2001* as:\n\n"*The reasonably probable and legal use of vacant land or an improved property, that is physically possible, appropriately supported, and financially feasible and that results in the highest value*".\n\n<a id=\'06d7df18-194f-4dad-895f-ecc34de28c34\'></a>\n\nThe following tests must be met in estimating the highest and best use. The use must be legal; the use\nmust be probable, not speculative or conjectural. There must be a profitable demand for such use and it must\n\n<a id=\'20fd54b4-006a-4bb3-84fd-d56609156b11\'></a>\n\n12\n\n<a id=\'15f70b64-45c5-406b-b61f-3199c7f2756d\'></a>\n\nreturn to the land the highest net return for the longest period of time.\n\n*   Legally Permissible Use – What uses are permitted legally under existing zoning, building codes, environmental regulations, and public/private deed restrictions?\n*   Physically Possible Use – What uses of the site are physically possible, given its size, shape, area, terrain, soils, ingress/egress, and assembly potential?\n*   Financially Feasible Use – Which possible and permissible uses will produce a positive net return to the owner of the property?\n*   Maximally Productive Use – Considering all feasible uses, which use will produce the highest residual land value consistent with the rate of return warranted by the market for that use?\n\n<a id=\'c8bfb54d-ce29-43c6-9ef0-7461f497b32a\'></a>\n\n## Legal Permissibility\n\nThe zoning of this parcel is Rural Residential Five Acre (RR-5) by the Yuba County Planning Department. This zoning allows for a density of one residential unit per five acres within the required setbacks and other criteria. The subject area is 17± acres and will support one single-family residence on the parcel as it exists now, per the Yuba County zoning designation as a **legally permissible** use. The parcel can also be subdivided into 3 smaller 5 acre lots, per the Yuba County Planning. Agricultural uses are also permitted within the RR-5 zoning ordinance. This eliminates any commercial, industrial or other uses on the subject property.\n\n<a id=\'34815a61-59df-4461-9495-938fe2470d86\'></a>\n\n## Physically Possible\n\nThe subject site is typical in size compared to the surrounding parcels with level topography. The size and shape of the parcel are functional and would **physically** allow for most types of residential structures, and small agricultural uses.\n\n<a id=\'a1cff982-7c5c-4d6d-93e9-c9913440ba56\'></a>\n\nFinancially Feasible\nThe determination of financial feasibility is based primarily on demand. The subject is located near recent land divisions for residential use. There is also ample agricultural activity in the region. Therefore, it would be financially feasible to obtain this parcel for a residential home, or agricultural site.\n\n<a id=\'bdfa8a8e-7725-4f24-ab17-916da36aeaa0\'></a>\n\n13\n\n<a id=\'36060946-37d2-498a-8bfd-f48f082c120a\'></a>\n\nMaximally Productive\nAfter evaluation of the legally permissible, physically possible, and financially feasible uses, the maximally productive use of the subject property is as Rural Residential Five Acres, with the primary use as a home site.\n\n<a id=\'0f02e5d9-0162-48a6-8ca9-2c616672bf1a\'></a>\n\nHIGHEST AND BEST USE CONCLUSION – AS THOUGH VACANT\n\n<a id=\'da6df6b6-dc76-4729-bd0d-838bd9e1291e\'></a>\n\nThe appraiser has performed the four tests of highest and best use as though vacant. The conclusion of highest and best use as vacant is Rural Residential.\n\n<a id=\'1e62d760-ede3-4e0e-84cc-6137a642b1b4\'></a>\n\n## METHODOLOGY\n\n### Sales Comparison for Land Value\n\nThere are six land valuation techniques recognized by the Appraisal Institute. These are sales comparison, allocation, extraction, subdivision development, land residual, and ground rent capitalization. The sales comparison approach is the most common and preferred method when sufficient market data is available. The appraiser has sufficient comparable market data, and therefore will rely solely on the sales comparison approach in deriving a unit value. This involves analyzing and comparing the sales of comparable properties, then adjusting them to the subject property to estimate value.\n\n<a id=\'4e8ebd47-ee2d-49a5-8149-852f99789e58\'></a>\n\n## LAND VALUATION\n\nIn determining the site value, vacant land sales used in valuing the subject encompassed the city of Smartsville and surrounding areas. Sources used were the Yuba County Assessor\'s files, Landvision® and interviews with real estate agents in the area.\n\n<a id=\'28a12590-b788-45eb-9b5c-4bec00e56a88\'></a>\n\nAll sales used were cash or cash equivalent sales; therefore no finance adjustments were necessary. The listing also offered no special financing. The market data used in this section sold from August 2014 to the current listing. Discussions with the Assessor\'s office and other brokers in the area indicate there has not been a significant change in rural residential property values over this period, therefore no adjustments for market conditions were made to the first 3 comparables. The comparables used have the same zoning as the subject and have similar utility as the subject property. All comparables used were also located in areas of custom homes with views of the surrounding mountains or valleys. All sites have been perc/mantle tested for septic, and included power on site. These comparables were chosen mainly based on size and location, and will be discussed below and analyzed on the spreadsheet on the opposite page.\n\n<a id=\'caec08b3-4cc9-48ba-8ca6-5f90c5011643\'></a>\n\n14\n\n<a id=\'b03a5136-e7c5-4a04-8585-ba022f1cba7f\'></a>\n\nCOMPARABLE SALES DATA GRID\n\n<a id=\'1644ea91-40c0-4fa7-a2a9-bad23547f567\'></a>\n\n15\n\n<a id=\'5d93b0ed-dd68-4039-84fd-5d4ccffd0bab\'></a>\n\n## DISCUSSION OF ADJUSTMENTS FOR SALES COMPARISON APPROACH\n\nAfter speaking with brokers, realtors, and the Yuba County Tax Assessor\'s office about the values added by different property characteristics in the Smartsville area, it was concluded that access to the NID irrigation ditch adds 15% to a property\'s value, a capped-well with no electrical or pump adds $6,000.00, and a completed perc/mantle test adds $5,000.00. After an analysis of listed and actual sale price in the Smartsville area, a 5% reduction in listing prices was deemed reasonable to adjust listings to market value. Through an analysis of available comparables, and interviews with sellers, a 10% adjustment is necessary to reflect the decreased value of properties that have their only access through a road easement over another parcel.\n\n<a id=\'d9af9384-4deb-4564-acdc-c64d8382b693\'></a>\n\nComparable 1 is an August 2014 sale of a vacant 19.63 acre parcel located west of the subject, in the community of Smartsville. According to the Yuba County Planning Department, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. Access is via McGanney Lane. Electric and telephone are to the site. There is a domestic well on site and it has two approved septic areas. It has rights to the NID for irrigation purposes but currently does not draw from the ditch. This was a private sale with seller financing; no broker was involved. According to the sellers, the transaction is considered an arm\'s length transaction and reflective of the market. A downward adjustment of $10,000.00 was made to Comparable 1 to reflect the added value the perc/mantles contributed to the comparable and a downward adjustment of $6,000.00 was made to reflect the added value of the capped-well. After all the adjustments were applied, the site\'s raw land value is $243,000.00.\n\n<a id=\'ee0e0578-7712-4419-9817-7f2d69a32e4e\'></a>\n\nComparable 2 is an August 2014 sale of a vacant 20.32-acre parcel located northwest of the subject property, across SR20, in the community of Smartsville. According to the Yuba County Planning Department, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. Access is via a road easement to McGanney Lane. Electric and telephone are to the site. The site does not have a domestic well but does have one approved septic area. It has rights to the Nevada Irrigation Ditch (NID) for irrigation purposes but currently does not draw from the ditch. This was a private sale with seller financing; no broker was involved. According to the sellers, the transaction is considered an arm\'s length transaction and reflective of the market. The sale price included $62,600.00 paid by the buyer to improve McGanney Lane and install a fire suppression pond for the seller to allow the 80 acres to be subdivided by Yuba County requirements; this is reflected in the "Adjustement for Expenditure as Condition of Escrow". A downward adjustment of $5,000.00 was made to Comparable 2 to reflect the added value the perc/mantle contributed to the comparable. An upwards adjustment of 10% was made to the properties access for having access only through a road easement from another parcel. After all the adjustments were applied, the property\'s site value is approximately $242,100.00.\n\n<a id=\'460fe85b-2abc-441e-8353-bfa5ee824773\'></a>\n\nComparable 3 is an August 2014 sale of a vacant 20.00-acre parcel located 0.1 miles west of the subject in the community of Smartsville. According to the sellers, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. Access is via a road easement to McGanney Lane. Electric and telephone are to the site. The site has one domestic well and three approved septic areas. It has rights to the Nevada Irrigation Ditch (NID) for irrigation purposes but currently does not draw from the ditch. The sale price included $62,600.00 paid by the buyer to improve McGanney Lane and install a fire suppression pond for the seller to allow the 80 acres to be subdivided by Yuba County requirements; this is reflected in the "Adjustment for Expenditure as Condition of Escrow". A downward adjustment of $15,000.00 was made to Comparable 3 to reflect the added value the perc/mantles contributed to the comparable and a downwards adjustment of $6,000.00 was made to reflect the added value of the capped-well. An upwards adjustment of 10% was made to the parcel\'s access for having access only through a road easement from another parcel. After all the adjustments were applied, the property\'s site value is approximately $234,400.00.\n\n<a id=\'4398d33f-f2db-49d7-a457-d39931b7f0ca\'></a>\n\n16\n\n<a id=\'858a0b3b-5220-4314-8ad4-03c29bb23a36\'></a>\n\nComparable 4 is a current listing of a vacant 20.42-acre parcel located 1.9 miles southwest of the subject within the Smartsville community boundary. According to the Yuba County Planning Department, this comparable is zoned Rural Residential (RR5) and has a minimum lot size of 5 acres. It is irregular in shape with a hilly topography. The parcel has frontage along Hammonton-Smartsville Road and Seven Moons Lanes. Electric and telephone are to the site. The site has one domestic well and one approved septic area. The parcel resides outside the Nevada Irrigation Ditch (NID) service district, but the Railroad Commissions Act does allow access to NID water; however, due to the distance between the parcel and the NID irrigation ditch, this parcel is to be viewed as being unable to access the NID in a manner that makes economic sense being that the closest NID ditch is approximately 3,200 feet to the northeast across several other parcels. Through an analysis of surrounding area listing and sales prices, it was determined that a 5% reduction on the listing price was needed to normalize the listing price to reflect a market transaction. A downward adjustment of $5,000.00 was made to Comparable 4 to reflect the added value the perc/mantle contributed to the comparable and a downward adjustment of $6,000.00 to reflect the added value of the capped-well. An upwards adjustment of 15% was made to the property\'s value to reflect the inability to effectively hook-up to the NID irrigation ditch. After all the adjustments were applied, the property\'s site value is approximately $241,900.00.\n\n<a id=\'f44b48fb-c408-46a7-b5ef-611e2dc9b728\'></a>\n\nRECONCILIATION OF UNIT VALUE\n\nTheThe market data comparables were analyzed and resulted in a site range of $234,400.00 to $243,000.00 for the subject property. All comparables were weighted relatively equally against each other with an emphasis placed on comparable 1 because it required the least amount of adjustments of the comparables. Each were similar to the subject in respect to their utility, located in the immediate area of the subject property, and are representative of the current market. With the above analysis in mind, the appraiser has estimated the land value of the subject to be $243,000.00 as vacant.\n\n<a id=\'8c43701a-22e5-47ca-a07d-146575aa4b13\'></a>\n\n17\n\n<a id=\'8beb4e2a-8409-47bb-a5e0-30ba12e18851\'></a>\n\nTHE ACQUISITION\n\n<a id=\'d659ee50-95fe-474d-bc05-f213bc17d0e7\'></a>\n\nThe State\'s acquisition consists of underlying fee under the current right of way and a fee parcel that runs along the northern edge of the subject adjacent to State Route 20. This fee parcel (Parcel 36668-1 on the R/W maps) consists of 72,851 SF of the parcel\'s northern border. This area is needed to accommodate the new SR20 alignment to lessen the severity of the curve at the subject\'s location, allow for a 4:1 slope along the highway, and extend the shoulders to 8\' wide. The fee acquisition will leave the parcel with a remainder of 667,669 SF, or 15.33 acres. The 40,826 SF of underlying fee area on State Route 20 (shown on the R/W maps) as Parcel 36668-1 is the State\'s existing right of way and is held in Highway easement. Since it is encumbered, and holds no utility to the property owner, it will be appraised at $1.00.\n\n<a id=\'bc75c946-c750-40ab-abfe-92dbeac82369\'></a>\n\nWith that said, a site value of $243,000.00 was determined in the previous section for the land value.\nFor calculating purposes, an overall square foot value will be used. The determination of the overall square\nfoot value is as follows:\n\n<a id=\'15eeb8cb-48c8-402a-afad-f4f89daf3b31\'></a>\n\n$243,000.00 ÷ 740,520 SF (site size) = $0.33/SF\n\n<a id=\'2b19905c-6e7b-41b6-8dbd-864b5dc19ce3\'></a>\n\n<table id="17-1">\n<tr><td id="17-2" colspan="2">Calculations for these parcels are as follows:</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-3">Parcel 36668-1 (Fee Acquisition)</td><td id="17-4"></td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-5">72,851 @ $0.33/SF</td><td id="17-6">= $24,040.83</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-7">Parcel 36668-1 (Underlying Fee)</td><td id="17-8"></td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-9">20,178 SF @ $1.00</td><td id="17-a">= $1.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="17-b">Total Land Value</td><td id="17-c">$24,041.83</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'c595ad64-31d1-4a97-8a46-41d07c212cae\'></a>\n\n18\n\n<a id=\'c1fa739b-c957-4073-8682-9a869eca3fd5\'></a>\n\nIMPROVEMENTS\nThe improvements in the proposed acquisition area consist of approximately 1,040 linear feet of 4-strand-barbed-wire fence, 5 strand barbed-wire fence, and wire mesh fence with 2 strand barbed-wire. For the purpose of this appraisal, the highest price per unit of the 3 types was used to calculate, that being the wire mesh on steel posts with 2 strands of barbed-wire. To obtain a price for wire mesh fencing with 2 strand barbed-wire across the top in the Smartsville area, Action Fencing of Marysville was contacted. During conversations with the contractor, it was deemed that $8.00/LF was the cost for wire mesh fencing with 2 strand barbed-wire. During inspection of the property and the fencing, it was observed to be 50% depreciated, that is to say that 50% of its useful life is remaining. Approximately 197 LF of shared 5 strand barbed-wire fencing is to be acquired, and this value will be split between the two respective owners. During inspection of the property and the fencing, it was observed to be 50% depreciated, that is to say that 50% of its useful life is remaining.\n\n<a id=\'c65fbbde-5bad-4939-81ca-5ac50f96ce83\'></a>\n\n<table id="18-1">\n<tr><td id="18-2" colspan="2">Fencing Improvements</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-3" colspan="2">Fencing (wire mesh on steel posts)</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-4">- 1,040 LF x $8.00/LF</td><td id="18-5">$ 8,320.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-6">Depreciation (50% x $8,320.00)</td><td id="18-7">$ 4,160.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-8">Fencing Total</td><td id="18-9">$ 4,160.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-a" colspan="2">Fencing (shared barbed-wire)</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-b">-½ (197 LF x $6.22/LF)</td><td id="18-c">$ 612.67</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-d">Depreciation (50% x $612.67)</td><td id="18-e">$ 306.33</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-f">Fencing Total</td><td id="18-g">$ 306.34</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="18-h">Final Improvements Value</td><td id="18-i">$ 4,466.34</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'81e47563-ae2d-4df0-b903-eb439d8b4646\'></a>\n\n19\n\n<a id=\'e47200f7-af98-4d77-af8a-89eac5131faf\'></a>\n\nREMAINDER – DAMAGES AND BENEFITS\n\n1 ... [illegible]\n\n<a id=\'1f98164d-3030-4037-8599-1ed37c152b97\'></a>\n\nThe costs per unit were explained, and calculated, in the improvements section were used for calculating the damages as well. Depreciation of the improvements, for the purpose of the calculation of damages, was explained, and used, in the Improvement section as well. Approximately 1,040 linear feet of the existing wire mesh fencing will need to be replaced to bring the parcel to the same utility as the before condition; this is calculated new at $8,320.00 ($8.00/LF X 1,040 LF). Of this amount, the depreciated value in place was already paid in the improvements section in the amount of $4,160.00 ($8,320.00 X 50%). The cost to cure was calculated as $4,160.00 ($8,320.00 X 50%). Due to the acquisition, an additional 70 LF of fencing will be required to be installed on the northern border to restore utility to the parcel. This was calculated with a replacement cost new of $560.00 ($8.00/LF X 70 LF).\n\n<a id=\'df15ff2b-dfc8-4592-bc8c-248c5e19b638\'></a>\n\nA contingency fee of 15% will be added to the replacement cost new (shown below) to account for\nany oversight by the grantor, or unforeseen labor or material costs.\n\n<a id=\'3dab9aea-ea22-4f3f-9646-942090b65a97\'></a>\n\n<table id="19-1">\n<tr><td id=\'faceeab5-c2ac-4371-81e2-7183ad5fb9fa\'></a>\n\nRECAPITULATION\n\n<a id=\'906a90b7-a094-40d8-8edb-e1b984683069\'></a>\n\n<table id="20-1">\n<tr><td id="20-2">Land</td><td id="20-3">= $ id="20-h"></td><td id="20-i">$34,600.00</td><td id="20-j">(Rounded)</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'591298c8-246c-4f86-8a6c-f49b07aaa700\'></a>\n\n**CONSTRUCTION CONTRACT WORK**\n\nAccording to Caltrans Design Engineer Kevin Lee, there is no Construction Contract work needed for this parcel.\n\n<a id=\'f4774eb9-bec1-4bd7-bcbe-b04e936f250f\'></a>\n\nSUMMARY OF THE BASIS FOR JUST COMPENSATION\n\nThe sales comparison approach was used to determine land value due to comparable sale availability and similarity to the subject. The cost approach was used to determine the replacement cost of the fencing improvements that fell in the acquisition area. Costs were obtained from The Marshall & Swift (M&S) Residential Cost Handbook, and estimates from local contractors. Curable damages were valued by the replacement cost of a new fence minus the improvements\' depreciated value in place. No incurable damages will be sustained from the partial acquisition as the remainder will not lose any utility. No special benefits were noted as a result of the proposed project.\n\n<a id=\'6dadee37-1930-4b70-874b-acb73609abc4\'></a>\n\n21\n\n<a id=\'d95a4ab4-9f3c-419e-aee0-7ef13b1eaef8\'></a>\n\n# APPENDIX\n* Comparable Data Summary Page\n* Comparable Data Map\n* Comparable Data Sheets\n* Comparable Tax Assessor Maps\n* Appraisal Terms (3 pgs.)\n* R/W Engineering Appraisal Map (1 pg.)\n\n<a id=\'e015bd11-2a18-4768-9d42-3d8586458e70\'></a>\n\n22\n\n<a id=\'f94c0bd1-3ea0-4887-9a9d-915bb10b4621\'></a>\n\nCOMPARABLE SUMMARY PAGE\n\n<a id=\'fb5be767-9b1c-40ac-828c-519112b4597f\'></a>\n\n<table id="22-1">\n<tr><td id="22-2">Comp No.</td><td id="22-3">C.O.E.</td><td id="22-4">Location</td><td id="22-5">Price</td><td id="22-6">Site Size</td><td id="22-7">Price Per Site</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-8">1</td><td id="22-9">08/03/14</td><td id="22-a">McGanney Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-b">$ 259,000.00</td><td id="22-c">19.63 Acres</td><td id="22-d">$ 259,000.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-e">2</td><td id="22-f">08/03/14</td><td id="22-g">McGanney Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-h">$ 225,100.00</td><td id="22-i">20.32 Acres</td><td id="22-j">$ 225,100.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-k">3</td><td id="22-l">08/11/14</td><td id="22-m">McGanney Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-n">$ 234,100.00</td><td id="22-o">20.00 Acres</td><td id="22-p">$ 234,100.00</td></tr>\n<tr><td id="22-q">4</td><td id="22-r">Listing</td><td id="22-s">Seven Moons Lane Smartsville, CA 95977</td><td id="22-t">$ 233,000.00</td><td id="22-u">20.42 Acres</td><td id="22-v">$ 233,000.00</td></tr>\n</table>\n\n<a id=\'edb979ab-61a1-4d7a-9b8b-d5884cbf72b3\'></a>\n\n23\n\n<a id=\'9a5b16b2-8466-48b0-875f-8f093ae5fe6f\'></a>\n\nCOMPARABLE MAP SHEET\n\n<a id=\'02ac30b9-b890-43c5-873b-30dcbae75a0e\'></a>\n\n<::Aerial map showing properties and comparable listings.
